<div id="review_191831442" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191831442" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191831442?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780739465516" href="/book/show/79885.The_Lincoln_Lawyer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191831442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1075985761224016487">I got the idea to read this from Nicholson Baker's article against Amazon's Kindle device where he said he had to finish reading this on his Kindle (despite disliking doing so on such a shoddy device) because he had to know what happened in the end. I'm not predisposed toward legal/crime thrillers as I think they're a bit too melodramatic and sensationalist (I was thinking of John Grisham). However it's an unfair generalisation as I hadn't read any books from this genre. So I picked it up not ex</span>
  <span id="freeText1075985761224016487" style="display:none">I got the idea to read this from Nicholson Baker's article against Amazon's Kindle device where he said he had to finish reading this on his Kindle (despite disliking doing so on such a shoddy device) because he had to know what happened in the end. I'm not predisposed toward legal/crime thrillers as I think they're a bit too melodramatic and sensationalist (I was thinking of John Grisham). However it's an unfair generalisation as I hadn't read any books from this genre. So I picked it up not expecting much, probably giving up after the court room scene where the lawyer does a Pacino and spouts on to the jury about how the system is corrupt, etc. Yawn, snooze. <br /><br />What can I say? Pleasantly surprised? No, in fact utterly gobsmacked! What had I been missing! Who was this writer?! Michael Connelly... the name was one of those you see in charity shelves alongside James Patterson and Andy McNab, an ubiquitous author, bound to be overpraised. I'd say "The Lincoln Lawyer" is the best novel I've read in a year. <br /><br />I can't complain about any aspect of the book - the characters were solid, the main character utterly likeable, believable and real, the plot compelling, the dialogue and descriptions, right down to the legal speak seemed authoritative and right (I'm not a lawyer so I can only say it sounded like he'd done his research). The whole setup of a lawyer in a lincoln town car, the pro with years of experience dealing with judges and bikers with complete confidence, was new to me and rich in story. Even Nicholson Baker's claim that he read the last hundred pages at a gallop in one sitting turned out true - actually for me it was more like the last 150 pages in one enjoyable sunny Sunday afternoon. <br /><br />I cannot recommend this book more. I'm not one for legal thrillers but this was a fantastic novel. I'm already deep into the sequel "The Brass Verdict" and have ordered Connelly's latest "The Scarecrow". I urge you to check this guy out, the man knows how to write. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1075985761224016487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6892289794340388883" style="display:none">I'm a big fan of Michael Connelly, and this is one of his best. So many unexpected twists, terrific audio performance, and the pages just effortlessly keep turning. Also, Connelly doesn't drift down the sex and violence and gore hallways when he writes thrillers. He keeps those things to a minimum, considering that the book is, in essence, a murder mystery. This is something I really appreciate. <br /><br />I find myself completely, happily immersed whenever I pick up one of his books. If you've never tried Connelly, this is the first of a series starring defense attorney Mickey Haller. Every book in the series is at least a four-star read. Imo, this is the best of them. Hard to go wrong with any one of his books. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2519460374" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2518815093454218203">For this first book in this series, author Connelly dreams up a bizarre, convoluted legal situation that really should be a 1990s movie starring Ashley Judd and Tommie Lee Jones. It's easy to read though, with a plot that moves quickly along and plenty of snappy dialogue to go with the contrived dramatic situations and ridiculous coincidences. Ultimately, it's fun if you don't think about it too hard.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22594333-fred?shelf=movie">movie</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2621690255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8091237910272093004">*<br/><a href='http://www.hawes.com/2005/2005-10-23.pdf' rel='nofollow noopener'>NYT Best Seller List - 10/23/2005 - #1</a><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/8720.Best_by_Michael_Connelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Goodreads - Best by Michael Connelly list - #1</a><br/><a href='https://www.imdb.com/title/tt1189340/' rel='nofollow noopener'>IMDB - Book used in The Lincoln Lawyer movie</a><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=H27t-pYOavw' rel='nofollow noopener'>YouTube 🍿The Lincoln Lawyer movie trailer</a><br/><br/><a href='https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&rct=j&q=&esrc=s&source=web&cd=2&ved=2ahUKEwjjqYGiyYPnAhVOwlkKHVXwDpYQwqsBMAF6BAgKEAc&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fwatch%3Fv%3DL6P1WtMVa8s&usg=AOvVaw0_syTjXondSrbQp0LY6MWA%20' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lincoln Lawyer (2011) – Opening Title Sequence - great</a><br/><br/>The book is great but I liked the movie much more than most others do...<br/><br/>Micky Haller - The Lincoln Lawyer - in his expensive Lincoln Town car, charges high retainers & bails for clients to “Get out of jail” just like Monopoly. But you don’t get money back innocent or guil</span>
  <span id="freeText8091237910272093004" style="display:none">*<br><a href="http://www.hawes.com/2005/2005-10-23.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">NYT Best Seller List - 10/23/2005 - #1</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/8720.Best_by_Michael_Connelly" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads - Best by Michael Connelly list - #1</a><br><a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt1189340/" rel="nofollow noopener">IMDB - Book used in The Lincoln Lawyer movie</a><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=H27t-pYOavw" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube 🍿The Lincoln Lawyer movie trailer</a><br><br><a href="https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&amp;rct=j&amp;q=&amp;esrc=s&amp;source=web&amp;cd=2&amp;ved=2ahUKEwjjqYGiyYPnAhVOwlkKHVXwDpYQwqsBMAF6BAgKEAc&amp;url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fwatch%3Fv%3DL6P1WtMVa8s&amp;usg=AOvVaw0_syTjXondSrbQp0LY6MWA%20" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lincoln Lawyer (2011) – Opening Title Sequence - great</a><br><br>The book is great but I liked the movie much more than most others do...<br><br>Micky Haller - The Lincoln Lawyer - in his expensive Lincoln Town car, charges high retainers &amp; bails for clients to “Get out of jail” just like Monopoly. But you don’t get money back innocent or guilty, they are non-refundable, going to the Lawyer fee &amp; court.<br> <blockquote>
<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544496751i/26725920._SY540_.jpg" width="230" height="280" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>EXCELLENT movie - one of my favorites <br>
</blockquote><br>Regina Campo (prostitute) is found unconscious in her apartment brutally raped &amp; assaulted. Louis Roulet was found unconscious in the apartment too. A knife with his prints &amp; blood found. The Lamplighter Bar has a Video tape of her passing a note to meet. He says it was a setup. Mary Windsor (mom) never likes Micky after meeting him.<br><br>Roulet turns down Ted Minton, district attorney (DA - chief prosecutor) offers a 7 year sentence, out in 4, jail sentence. Roulet only wants to plead innocence, pays bail to get out &amp; wait for trial.<br><br>Raul Levin, Haller’s chief investigator &amp; close friend is killed. Police search Micky’s home &amp; find a .22 caliber Colt Woodsman Sport Model pistol that would be like a .22 pistol used in his murder. But they find it’s empty wooden box? Was it the gun used in the murder?<br><br>During the trial, DJ Corliss, a “jail house snitch” says Roulet confessed to him. Mitch’s support is for “Snitches” like Roulet get info for prosecutors as favors in their upcoming trials. But Micky Haller makes the lie backfire on Minton (DA) when evidence shows DJ Corliss lied many times in the past. Prosecution called for “misconduct” &amp; Roulet’s released innocent.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Helped from another snitch immediately arrests Roulet “Murder”? But not enough evidence to arrest again?<br>Is Roulet’s family, Maggie (x-wife, District DA) &amp; Hayley (daughter) under threat? <br>What crimes could Louis Roulet? Mary Windsor(mom) have committed &amp; arrested?<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><blockquote>
<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544794551i/26744226._SX540_.jpg" width="375" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Matthew McConaughey<br>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_300339587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300339587" />
    <a title="Cathy DuPont" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6637209-cathy-dupont"><img alt="Cathy DuPont" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393680963p2/6637209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300339587?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy DuPont" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy DuPont" href="/user/show/6637209-cathy-dupont">Cathy DuPont</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6365855-the-lincoln-lawyer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6637209-cathy-dupont?shelf=noir-favorites">noir-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300339587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8662881900426093993">WOW! What a great read that was. Great plot; clear and interesting characters; action, something happening every page; twists and turns; did I say great plot? <br/><br/>To me it was one of the best books I've read in a long time and a first for me reading Michael Connelly. I've seen his name and books but never been too interested in the hyped and hightly marketed authors which I thought defined Connelly. I was just plain wrong. Connelly writes like I like and enjoy. He writes like a professional, clear a</span>
  <span id="freeText8662881900426093993" style="display:none">WOW! What a great read that was. Great plot; clear and interesting characters; action, something happening every page; twists and turns; did I say great plot? <br /><br />To me it was one of the best books I've read in a long time and a first for me reading Michael Connelly. I've seen his name and books but never been too interested in the hyped and hightly marketed authors which I thought defined Connelly. I was just plain wrong. Connelly writes like I like and enjoy. He writes like a professional, clear and clean. So I'm now on the Connelly band wagon. <br /><br />This new character, Michael "Mickey" Haller is a defense attorney and apparently the step brother to another established character who Connelly has been writing about for quite some time. A guy by the name of Bosch. <br /><br />I caught this right since I like reading from the beginning rather than starting a series in the middle. <br /><br />Most of Haller's clients appear to be guilty and he just 'finds a crack' which opens up a gray area of doubt which keeps them from prison. He's troubled that he may not recognize innocence when he sees it and he carries that as a very heavy burden. <br /><br />Having the 'perfect' client who can move him finanically to the top, the client quickly becomes a burden and places Haller in a untenable situation. <br /><br />Great book, skillful writing and a pleasure to read. Could hardly put the book down and looking forward to reading more of Connelly, hyped or not. I think not. He's too good so it's not hype.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8662881900426093993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6142248-magdalena?shelf=am">am</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330697628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12754638082012576111">"The Lincoln Lawyer" is a gripping, character driven thriller, full of twists and turns that kept me interested right till the end. <br/>Haller is one of those characters that you cannot help but like. He is full of attitude, charisma and charm that allows him to use and manipulate the system just enough to make money and keep clients knocking on his door. With Haller it is not so much about justice as making the system work in your favour. <br/>And then that one case lands in his lap, the case that makes</span>
  <span id="freeText12754638082012576111" style="display:none">"The Lincoln Lawyer" is a gripping, character driven thriller, full of twists and turns that kept me interested right till the end. <br />Haller is one of those characters that you cannot help but like. He is full of attitude, charisma and charm that allows him to use and manipulate the system just enough to make money and keep clients knocking on his door. With Haller it is not so much about justice as making the system work in your favour. <br />And then that one case lands in his lap, the case that makes things personal. Haller must throw everything he knows and learnt over the years to save himself, in more ways than one. <br />I have to say I loved how well Connelly wrote that story, it is not perfect, there are some flaws in plot but it is a great story and definitely worth reading.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer989961821331104948">I admit having seen the movie with Mathew M. quite some time ago and finding it an enjoyable movie, a bit surprised there has not been a sequel as there are more books out there with the same character. That said the movie version was a much slicker person as the book person, and I enjoyed the book better than the movie.<br/><br/>This is one of those books you want to keep reading even if you are aware that you have important stuff to do, you keep reading on. I have seen the movie but forgot most of the p</span>
  <span id="freeText989961821331104948" style="display:none">I admit having seen the movie with Mathew M. quite some time ago and finding it an enjoyable movie, a bit surprised there has not been a sequel as there are more books out there with the same character. That said the movie version was a much slicker person as the book person, and I enjoyed the book better than the movie.<br /><br />This is one of those books you want to keep reading even if you are aware that you have important stuff to do, you keep reading on. I have seen the movie but forgot most of the plot so the book kept me guessing. Having read some of the Bosch novels I was somewhat aware about the writing-skill and abilties of the writer who did not let me down with this new series. Of which I am quite sure I will read the sequels hoping that they like the Bosch novels will remain their quality.<br /><br />A very enjoyable hard-to-lay-down-novel of a writer I have enjoyed since I got the book "the Poet" from my mother after her visit to the USA. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QK8AbT+bAwI8kf8EFTaf584dtTPS7MhazmaeVG8dinsSjhj3CAHq9q4sCn/voO2PBwyNuJO/pUb8GNi/VFO+wg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vlhh80PTjVRw6euT1PqWkSn0JQXqjY7OtXyXYZWbX9LseXlpdElkoOJUHugubOT54OUdjqve49KHAtGKrtVraw==')})
  }

None of the gritty darkness or frenzied action is lost in 1st to Die, although the female protagonists offer an even deeper emotional context to this suspense thriller.\n\nInspector Lindsay Boxer of the San Francisco Police Department suddenly finds herself in the middle of two horrifying situations: The first is that she\'s just learned she has an often-fatal blood disease. The second is a double homicide case she is now heading up that involves the murder of newlyweds on their wedding night. Burdened with Chris Raleigh, a new partner reassigned from the mayor\'s office, Lindsay finds that she has too much to deal with and turns to her best friend, Claire, the head ME on the case. Claire offers helpful advice and human, friendly contact amid a job filled with violence, cruelty, and fear.\n\nSoon a fledgling newspaper reporter, Cindy, makes contact with Lindsay looking for a career-making story. Although Lindsay can\'t officially comment on the case, the two women form a rapport, and Cindy joins Lindsay and Claire for their weekly meeting. When a second pair of newlyweds is murdered, and later a third, the investigation leads to a prominent crime writer, Nicholas Jenks, who has a history of spousal abuse and a predilection for kinky, dangerous sex games. With the help of an understanding assistant D.A., Jill Bernhardt, Lindsay tries to make a case against Jenks, who even had an affair with one of the slain women. Eventually Jill joins the Murder Club, and the four ladies share private interdepartmental information in an effort to track and stop the killer before he strikes again.\n\nThe major subplot -- Lindsay\'s facing up to her illness even while she learns to fall in love again -- carefully compensates for the novel\'s coarse scenes of brutality. Lindsay Boxer is\'t merely an obsessed cop trailing a maniac; she\'s also a terrified woman confronting the onslaught of disease. The story lines balance out to show us the true mettle of someone who puts the safety of others before her own.\n\nAgain, Patterson\'s skill for producing furiously paced fiction are evident as the novel breezes by rapidly. The short chapters keep the narrative leaping with increasingly taut plot elements, but there\'s an emotional commitment that makes our protagonist even more amiable and involving. 1st to Die is a novel that works as an intense series of character portraits that will leave the reader touched and delighted.\n\n--Tom Piccirilli<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"13050658193114407177\" href=\"#\"           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15318629692977920364"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads' database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information.</a></i> <br/><br/>Michael Connelly decided to become a writer after discovering the books of Raymond Chandler while attending the University of Florida. Once he decided on this direction he chose a major in journalism and a minor in creative writing — a curriculum in which one of his teache</span>
  <span id="freeText15318629692977920364" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads' database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information.</a></i> <br /><br />Michael Connelly decided to become a writer after discovering the books of Raymond Chandler while attending the University of Florida. Once he decided on this direction he chose a major in journalism and a minor in creative writing — a curriculum in which one of his teachers was novelist Harry Crews.<br /> <br />After graduating in 1980, Connelly worked at newspapers in Daytona Beach and Fort Lauderdale, Florida, primarily specializing in the crime beat. In Fort Lauderdale he wrote about police and crime during the height of the murder and violence wave that rolled over South Florida during the so-called cocaine wars. In 1986, he and two other reporters spent several months interviewing survivors of a major airline crash. They wrote a magazine story on the crash and the survivors which was later short-listed for the Pulitzer Prize for feature writing. The magazine story also moved Connelly into the upper levels of journalism, landing him a job as a crime reporter for the Los Angeles Times, one of the largest papers in the country, and bringing him to the city of which his literary hero, Chandler, had written.<br /> <br />After three years on the crime beat in L.A., Connelly began writing his first novel to feature LAPD Detective Hieronymus Bosch. The novel, The Black Echo, based in part on a true crime that had occurred in Los Angeles, was published in 1992 and won the Edgar Award for Best First Novel by the Mystery Writers of America. Connelly has followed that up with over 30 more novels. <br /> <br />Over eighty million copies of Connelly’s books have sold worldwide and he has been translated into forty foreign languages. He has won the Edgar Award, Anthony Award, Macavity Award, Los Angeles Times Best Mystery/Thriller Award, Shamus Award, Dilys Award, Nero Award, Barry Award, Audie Award, Ridley Award, Maltese Falcon Award (Japan), .38 Caliber Award (France), Grand Prix Award (France), Premio Bancarella Award (Italy), and the Pepe Carvalho award (Spain) .<br /><br />Michael was the President of the Mystery Writers of America organization in 2003 and 2004. In addition to his literary work, Michael is one of the producers and writers of the TV show, “Bosch,” which is streaming on Amazon Prime Video. <br /><br />Michael lives with his family in Los Angeles and Tampa, Florida.</span>
